                                    <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><b>Wix is one of the only builders that lets you create exactly the website you want.</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> With the drag-and-drop editor, you can adjust the layout, change colors and fonts, add links and buttons, and much more.</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> If you have a really specific idea in mind for your site, you don’t have to start from scratch. <a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=2419&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_2419_top10_145_703938&post_id=145&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="2419" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_2419_top10_145_703938', 'wix', this,  true  );"><strong>Wix offers over 900 templates</strong></a></span><b> organized in 19 different categories and 70+ subcategories.</b></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">What that means, in short, is that </span><b>Wix has a template for just about any kind of website that you could think of</b><span style="font-weight: 400;">.</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> But you don’t even have to use the designated template for your industry. </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">Wix’s customization freedom meant that</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> I could just choose my favorite design and adjust it to meet my needs.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">If you ever need even more features for your site, </span><b>Wix offers a massive app market with over 250 native and third-party extensions.</b> <span style="font-weight: 400;">Many of the apps are free, and you can use them to add things as basic as simple contact forms or social media integrations </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">to more advanced functionalities like</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> full-blown </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">e-commerce features or integrations for podcast feeds and livestreams.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">All of this might make it sound like Wix is made only for the tech-savvy, but that couldn’t be further from the truth. Whether you want to build an e-commerce site and sell online, take online books, create a portfolio or blog, or even take orders for your restaurant, Wix is incredibly easy to learn and use. Plus it has the business management tools to go with it. </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">And thanks to the free plan, you can try it out and even publish your site without paying a dime.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The one caveat is that it’s easy to get lost in all these features. I spent hours on my site, </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">not because I had to, but because there was so much to explore and I was enjoying the process so much. </span><b>Are there simpler builders out there? For sure</b><b>, but nothing is quite like Wix.</b></p>

                                    <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><strong>Squarespace is truly a beautiful website builder</strong>, both in the sites it creates and in the interface itself. It’s most similar to WordPress.com, with a block editor and similar navigation layout between pages and other design facets. However, I found the experience of building a site on Squarespace to be much smoother, like Wix, with everything a bit more connected in the interface.</p>
<p><strong>Where most website builders emphasize either content or e-commerce more strongly, <a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=2413&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_2413_top10_145_763268&post_id=145&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="2413" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_2413_top10_145_763268', 'squarespace', this,  true  );">Squarespace manages to shine in both aspects</a></strong>, making it a great option for e-commerce stores of any size that also want to prominently feature their blog. (You can do this on other builders too, but Squarespace has strong functionality for both, at a greater scale than say, Wix.)</p>
<p>Squarespace doesn’t have a free plan (although it does offer a 14-day free trial), but you can access the majority of essential features on either of the lower tier plans, which are comparably priced to the other builders on this list.</p>

<p>Shopify has too many e-commerce features to name.                                     <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><strong>Web.com is intuitive, versatile, and complete</strong>. The editor includes tools to edit each aspect of your site with varying levels of detail. This makes it surprisingly versatile for users of different levels of experience. If you’re a beginner, you could design a simple site in a few minutes or spend a little extra time fine-tuning it to your taste.</p>
<p>It also comes with useful tools for websites of any kind. Web.com offers easy-to-use but powerful features for SEO, marketing, e-commerce, blogging, and more. <strong>If you don’t want to bother with design, you can even pay a small fee to hire an expert web designer to create the ideal site for you.</strong> You can still use the classic editor once the designer delivers. That way, you get all the benefits of professional design while always keeping the final say over your site.</p>
<p>It’s not a perfect editor. The same versatility that makes it impressive doesn’t allow it to excel at anything in particular.</p>
<p>For example, the editor is easy to use, but it hasn’t been created with<i> </i>absolute<i> </i>beginners in mind. And though it offers a rather extensive set of features for e-commerce, it can’t compete with dedicated e-commerce builders. Still, <strong>if you’re an intermediate user looking for a flexible builder, Web.com is a strong contender.</strong></p>

Out WordPress                                                 </a>

                                    <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><span style="font-weight: 400;">WordPress.org is the old-school giant of content management and website creation. Old-school doesn’t mean out-of-use, however – about a third of all sites on the internet still run on WordPress. Thankfully, </span><b>WordPress.com makes the WordPress experience available for anyone </b>by removing the need to<span style="font-weight: 400;"> self-host or have advanced knowledge of web development.</span></p>
<p><b>WordPress.com is the website builder version of WordPress</b>,<span style="font-weight: 400;"> offering more intuitive access to most of WordPress’ features. That said, even this “easier website builder version” comes with a steep learning curve. On top of that, most of the really interesting features, like plugins and premium templates, are only accessible through the Pro plan.</span></p>
<p><strong>WordPress.com has one great thing going for it, though:</strong><b> it offers nearly limitless opportunities to expand. </b>That said,<span style="font-weight: 400;"> it’s far from the easiest or the cheapest website builder out there.</span></p>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">The WordPress.com block editor is a relatively new feature. It seems like a (mostly effective) attempt to make WordPress more intuitive and visual than the classic method of backend editing. The new editor uses blocks both to add content and to modify the layout of the page. It&#8217;s simple enough, but I found it a bit finicky at times. I had to re-do chunks of my site more than once, which could get a bit frustrating. </span></p>

                                    <div class="top10-vendor-list-item-content top10-content"><p><strong>Duda is a visual builder for agencies and independent professionals.</strong> That’s why you get full access to advanced design features (such as direct CSS editing and breakpoint editing) even on the cheapest plan. In fact, Duda is filled with features for client work, such as custom backend branding, and the ability to make simple changes to a site without breaking it.</p>
<p>Does that mean that it’s no use to the average user? Of course not! <strong>Though there is a steep-ish learning curve, Duda offers an accessible editor for anyone who likes web design – </strong>provided they’re willing to spend the time getting things right.</p>
<p>Duda’s Flex mode is pretty remarkable. It lets you customize your site by dragging and dropping pre-made sections or even editing CSS yourself.</p>
<p>I want to emphasize that using this builder involves a significant learning curve. Therefore, I wouldn&#8217;t suggest it for those who aren&#8217;t fully committed. Furthermore, although Duda offers good value for your investment, it&#8217;s important to note that it isn&#8217;t more affordable than its competitors and lacks a free plan.</p>

                <div class="top10-container">
                    <div class="top10-row top10-content">                            <h2 class="top10-section-desc-title" id="top10-section-desc-title">What I Looked For In The Best Website Builders</h2>                        <div class="top10-section-descBlock"><p></p> <span style="font-weight: 400;">I mostly focused</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> on three main criteria for comparison: ease of use, design flexibility, and pricing. There </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">were</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> some additional considerations as well, which helped to distinguish between</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> builders that scored pretty similarly on these main criteria.</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Here are the factors I considered when comparing the different website builders</span><span style="font-weight: 400;">:</span> 
<h3>Ease of Use</h3>
<p></p> <b>A good website builder will be intuitive, clear, and even enjoyable to use.</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Nearly all of these builders have some </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">sort of “getting started” tour.</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Once you are past the setup phase, all the tools you need should be </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">easy to find, and you shouldn’t have to struggle to learn what you can and can’t do with each of them. </span> 
<p></p> <strong>Editing the most crucial elements of a website </strong><span style="font-weight: 400;"><strong>should be easy.</strong> This means that customization options shouldn’t be</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> hidden behind several layers of navigation. Additionally, there should be clear and robust support options</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> that can provide timely answers.</span> 
<p></p> <strong><span style="font-weight: 400;">Bonus points </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">if a builder autosaves</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> your work and gives you continuous prompts for important steps, like publishing your website or connecting a domain.</span></strong> 
<h3>Design Flexibility</h3>
<p></p> <b>If you want</b><b> your site to stand out, </b><b>it can’t look like just another version of the same template visitors have seen a hundred times before.</b><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Chances are that you’ll have</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> to start from a template, but the best website builders will</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> not only give you a wide selection to choose from</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"><strong> (Wix, for example, gives you over 900)</strong>, </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">they will also give you the customization tools to transform it into something that has a distinctive look and unique identity.</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> Specifically, it should have:</span> 
<ul>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Plenty of initial templates to choose from</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Full control over color scheme</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">A wide range of fonts</span></li>
<li style="font-weight: 400;" aria-level="1"><span style="font-weight: 400;">Lots of options for page layouts and/or blocks</span></li>
</ul> <span style="font-weight: 400;">In my testing,</span><b> I noticed that drag-and-drop site editors tend to offer the most flexibility.</b> <span style="font-weight: 400;">You can see this in my</span><span style="font-weight: 400;"> test results, but other types of editors </span><span style="font-weight: 400;">can offer plenty of design freedom as well.</span> 
<h3>Pricing</h3>
<p></p> This criterion isn’t so much about absolute cost as it is about value. I ran a thorough website builder price comparison, and my conclusion was this: A site builder may have dirt cheap plans, but if its most expensive plan has only half the features you can find with a different builder’s most basic plan, that’s not really a point in its favor. 
<p></p> <strong>A good value website builder will give you the most features for the lowest cost</strong>. It may have a variety of plans to choose from, allowing you to customize to your needs. Squarespace, for instance, may not be the cheapest builder out there, but since it has so much to offer, I consider it excellent value. <a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=2413&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_2413_top10_145_483162&post_id=145&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="2413" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_2413_top10_145_483162', 'squarespace', this,  true  );">You can click here to see its latest plans.</a> 
<p></p> Often (but not always), the higher-tier plans are one of two things: more bandwidth and storage, or access to advanced e-commerce features. Having a sense of what your site will need will help you better assess the value of these plans as you read through the results. 
<h3>Additional Considerations</h3>
<p></p> While the criteria outlined above are the most important for comparing website builders, <strong>there are a few bonus features that I believe <b>help elevate some site builders above the rest.</b></strong> Any of these individually wouldn’t earn a builder a higher spot, but when combined with other strong features, they make these builders even more powerful. 
<p></p> These additional considerations must be actually useful &#8211; not just a flashy claim to good features. Here are some other things I looked at: 
<ul>
<li><strong>SEO capabilities</strong>: Most site builders help you optimize your title tags and meta descriptions, but the ones that have extra technical features, like auto-generating robots.txt files or sitemaps, are really helpful.</li>
<li><strong>Plenty of apps and integrations</strong>: This has more to do with function than design. A good site builder should be able to offer you the capabilities you need, ideally by integrating with other tools or software you’re already using, like MailChimp for email campaigns.</li>
<li><strong>A truly unique feature</strong>: Some builders have standout features that are unique to them and can’t really be compared with others. These are noted in the results for each builder.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="hselect-1">E-Commerce Builder or Regular Builder with E-Commerce Features?</h2>
<p></p> E-commerce builders, like the last three entries on our list, focus almost exclusively on the online store capabilities they offer. <strong>Their online store features surpass those of regular website builders by far</strong>, but you’ll find that nearly every other aspect of a website becomes somewhat unwieldy. 
<p></p> Regular website builders with e-commerce capabilities provide these features as more of an add-on than a primary service &#8211; although <strong>some &#8220;regular&#8221; builders,</strong> <strong>like Squarespace, have started offering very impressive e-commerce features</strong>. With these, it&#8217;s much easier to have a robust blog, a series of landing pages, and a high quantity of photos or videos. 
<p></p> I compared regular website builders and e-commerce builders, and I can say that there isn&#8217;t a single answer for all users. The<strong> type of builder you should choose depends on the primary purpose of your website</strong>. 
<p></p> If your main goal is to sell products, an e-commerce builder can provide you with extra payment options, easier upload and categorization of products, and sometimes even shipping deals. You don’t have to be a large retailer to benefit from one of these builders &#8211; Etsy sellers and local shops or boutiques may find a lot of advantages in one of these builders too. 
<p></p> But if you’re running a blog or personal site like a portfolio with the goal of selling just a few products, such as books or online courses, a regular builder with e-commerce features will provide more of what you need while still keeping your online store in shape. 
<p></p> <strong>Many e-commerce builders offer some kind of integration with other platforms or website builders, so your site can have the best of both worlds</strong>. If you are primarily a retailer but want to expand your site into a blog or other content, this combination may be the right choice. 
<h2 id="hselect-2">Website Builders Compared: The Testing Process</h2>
<p></p> To compare these website builders, I started with a framework for a simple site that would include features covering what most websites would consider the essentials. <strong>Every site I built had to include</strong>: 
<ul>
<li>Static text page (About page)</li>
<li>Blog post</li>
<li>Photo gallery</li>
<li>Calendar or event page</li>
<li>Contact page</li>
<li>Online store</li>
</ul> <strong>In addition, I would test the following functions</strong>: 
<ul>
<li>Changing color and font schemes</li>
<li>Adding images</li>
<li>Embedding video</li>
<li>Building a contact form</li>
<li>Adding a button</li>
<li>Editing a menu</li>
<li>Updating alt text</li>
<li>Testing SEO features</li>
</ul> This allowed me to test the most common website builder features, while spending enough time with each builder to make a thorough assessment of its capabilities. 
<p></p> Prior to building any websites, I compiled all of my resources and had a clear outline of what each page would entail, so I could build the exact same site with each tool. This cut out any time wasted thinking about what I wanted to include, hunting down images, and other setup needs. 
<p></p> <strong>I did not read any guides or watch any tutorials prior to building these sites</strong>, although I did have varying degrees of familiarity with some of the builders. I had previously used Wix and WordPress.com, although not extensively, and had done some research on the features for Squarespace, Weebly, and SITE123. 
<p></p> As I was building, if I ran into any issues I couldn’t figure out within the builder interface, I first checked the knowledge base and then reached out to support on either email or live chat. 
<h2 id="hselect-3">The Full Website Builder Comparison: How Each Builder Performed</h2>

<p></p> I used Google’s PageSpeed Insights to check which builders produce sites that just look pretty, and which are actually optimized for quick loading times. I tested the sites both on desktop and mobile. The scores you see here are between 1-100, with 100 being the highest possible.

<figure id="attachment_1520402" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1520402"class="wp-caption alignnone"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:69.992553983619% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-wix-2.png"  width="1343" height="940" alt="best-website-builders-wix-2" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-wix-2.png"   width="1343" height="940" alt="best-website-builders-wix-2" class="border wp-image-1520402 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1520402"class="wp-caption-text">My Wix website homepage (Template: Traveler Blog)</figcaption></figure>

<h4>Ease of Use</h4>
<p></p> <strong>The Wix website builder is truly the easiest and most intuitive site editor I tested</strong>. Everything I needed was in the first place I looked, and at no point did I feel frustrated or even need to check the support center for help. I was able to build about half of the site in just 30 minutes, and <strong>it took around 75 minutes to build</strong> <strong>my full Wix site</strong>. 
<p></p> To make it even easier, Wix has a whole suite of Artificial Intelligence (AI) features to help you create a website from scratch. <b>You’ll be asked a few questions about the site you want to create, and that’s it – Wix will then build you a custom site in minutes</b>. While there are some design limitations, you have full control to edit the site as you please. The AI can even import content from your social media accounts to make sure your branding is consistent. 
<p></p> You can then use more AI tools to help you write your website’s content, touch up images and analyze how your site is doing. And you can always revert back to an earlier version of your site whenever you want, as Wix saves everything. 
<p></p> First of all, all Wix sites are designed with best practices in mind to guarantee a solid SEO foundation. You’ll find that your site includes customizable meta tags, instant Google indexing, XML sitemaps, structured data markups and much more. All of this ensures it’s easy for people to find your site on search engines. You’ll also be able to connect your dashboard to Google Ads and Analytics so you can keep track of everything. 
<p></p> And if you’re completely lost, <strong>there’s an &#8216;SEO Setup Checklist’ to guide you through all the steps you need to complete &#8211; no prior SEO knowledge needed.</strong> I also love that Wix directs you to this feature by saying “Get Found On Google” &#8211; it makes it truly accessible to all. 
<figure id="attachment_3116500" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3116500"class="wp-caption alignnone"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:54.352941176471% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/SEO-setup-checklist-Wix-optimage2.png"  width="850" height="462" alt="A screenshot of Wix's SEO Setup Checklist" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/SEO-setup-checklist-Wix-optimage2.png"   width="850" height="462" alt="A screenshot of Wix's SEO Setup Checklist" class="size-full wp-image-3116500 ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3116500"class="wp-caption-text">My Wix SEO Setup Checklist</figcaption></figure> <strong>One drawback is that templates are not mobile-responsive</strong>, meaning they don’t automatically display perfectly on mobile devices. The base version of each template is mobile-friendly, but if you make a lot of changes to the desktop layout, you may need to separately edit your mobile site to ensure it appears correctly on mobile devices. 
<p></p> Many other website builders on this list have completely responsive templates, so there’s no need to double edit. My Wix site also loaded quite slowly on mobile during my page speed tests. 
<h4>Design Flexibility</h4>
<p></p> <strong>Wix certainly lives up to its promise of letting you edit every element of your site to customize it exactly how you want it</strong>. There are plenty of options for colors, font, blocks, and layouts, and you can save color palettes and font schemes easily for sitewide application. 
<figure id="attachment_3116618" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3116618"class="wp-caption alignnone"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:48.470588235294% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Wix-Layout-Options-optimage2.png"  width="850" height="412" alt="Wix Layout Options" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/Wix-Layout-Options-optimage2.png"   width="850" height="412" alt="Wix Layout Options" class="wp-image-3116618 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3116618"class="wp-caption-text">Wix has dozens of elements and layouts to add to your site</figcaption></figure> Built-in guidelines help you ensure your headings, images, and so on are aligned with each other. I sometimes had difficulty getting the drag-and-drop editor to do my bidding when fiddling with page height or other adjustments, but those are nearly at the pixel-level of adjustment and aren’t a big deal when considering the site design as a whole. 
<p></p> The huge number of templates helps you get this flexibility with less work upfront, since you are more likely to find a template that’s close to what you want on Wix than you are on another site builder. Unlike some other builders, <strong>most Wix templates are pretty distinctive</strong><strong>, so</strong> <strong>you’re not choosing a template because of its colors, but rather because of its functionality</strong>. You also have the option to start with a completely blank template and design the whole site from scratch. 
<p></p> <strong>Once you start editing a template, you can’t switch to a different one without starting over</strong>, so be sure of your choice before getting too far in designing. That said, since there is so much flexibility within the editor, you should be able to create anything you want within your chosen template, or even reproduce a layout from a different template that catches your eye later on. 
<h4>Pricing</h4>
<p></p> <strong>The Wix free plan gives you a lot of customization options</strong>, with access to all 900+ templates and a wide selection of apps. You can connect a custom domain on any plan, but if you want to accept online payments and integrate with Google Analytics, you’ll need to upgrade to a business plan. 
<p></p> Although there are various different plans, divided into Personal and Business &amp; E-commerce plans, there aren’t huge distinctions between most of them. Higher tiers are a big price jump for a little more storage and what they call “VIP Support.”

<h4>Other Features</h4>
<p></p> There are a few other notable things about Wix that I loved: 
<ul>
<li><strong>Online store</strong>: The Wix Store interface is really user friendly, walking you through every step of adding product information, shipping and payment options, and more. <span style="font-weight: 400;">You can also add apps to expand what your store can do, including things like Laybuy for flexible payments, Gifted for selling gift cards, and Shippo or ShipStation for printing shipping labels and getting lower shipping rates. </span></li>
<li><strong>Advanced SEO options</strong>: Beyond Wix SEO Wiz, the advanced SEO settings include options for structured data, canonical URLs, and custom meta tags. These help Google better understand your site on a technical level, without you having to take on any complex technical work. You can also set up AMP pages for a faster mobile experience.</li>
<li><strong>Support center</strong>: Wix offers 24/7 phone and live chat support as well as support through its social media channels where you can use “@WixHelp” on Twitter and Reddit. But you can also get VIP care and avoid any possible queues if you upgrade to a higher-tier plan. Although I didn’t ever need the support center, the information and support available is where Wix really shines. It has a ton of self-guided articles, video tutorials, and trending topics.</li>
<li><strong>Cutting-edge reliability and security:</strong> Wix does everything possible when it comes to keeping your website secure. It protects your website against attempts to steal sensitive data using the latest HTTPS security protocol and SSL certificate. And it has built-in solutions to prevent your site being knocked offline by cyberattacks (including DDoS attacks) and a dedicated incident response team that can get everything back up quickly should the worst happen.</li>
</ul>

<figure id="attachment_1520432" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1520432"class="wp-caption alignnone"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:65.727002967359% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-site123-2.png"  width="1348" height="886" alt="best-website-builders-site123-2" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-site123-2.png"   width="1348" height="886" alt="best-website-builders-site123-2" class="border wp-image-1520432 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1520432"class="wp-caption-text">My SITE123 test website homepage</figcaption></figure>

<h4>Ease of Use</h4>
<p></p> SITE123’s editor is simple to use and makes it easy to adjust your pages&#8230; if you know how it works. My site defaulted to a single page site, and it took me a good 20 minutes to figure out that when you add a block, you have to adjust its settings to not appear on the homepage but to remain in the navigation menus. Once I figured this out, <strong>building my SITE123 demo site went super fast. I build the complete site in under an hour</strong> (including the 20 minutes of troubleshooting). 
<figure id="attachment_1515803" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1515803"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 566px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:69.081272084806% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/site123-interface.png"  width="566" height="391" alt="SITE123’s interface for adding and reordering pages or sections" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/site123-interface.png"   width="566" height="391" alt="SITE123’s interface for adding and reordering pages or sections" class="border wp-image-1515803 size-full ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1515803"class="wp-caption-text">SITE123’s interface for adding and reordering pages or sections</figcaption></figure> In general, the interface isn’t completely intuitive: you may need to click around a bit to find exactly what you’re looking for. But if you run into a problem, the live chat is pretty responsive and helpful &#8211; they answered my question in less than 20 minutes. 
<p></p> The interfaces for each feature, like the blog and online store, are pretty straightforward to use. They don’t feel quite as modern as say, Wix or Squarespace, but that’s not a reflection on the look of the site this builder can produce. 
<h4>Design Flexibility</h4>
<p></p> You cannot customize your site as liberally on SITE123 as you can on Wix, but you can still customize a heck of a lot. <strong>There over 180 design templates to start with</strong>, as well as 14 categories of page layouts, including text, photo galleries, events, and even restaurant reservations. 
<p></p> These page types can be further customized by adding blocks, but you do hit some limitations based on the layout you choose. For example, I had chosen an About page template but was not able to embed a video as intended. I asked chat support, and was told that embedding a video was only allowed on certain page types: 
<figure id="attachment_1515834" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1515834"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 400px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:126.75% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/site123-live-chat-support.png"  width="400" height="507" alt="SITE123’s live chat support feature" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/site123-live-chat-support.png"   width="400" height="507" alt="SITE123’s live chat support feature" class="border wp-image-1515834 ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1515834"class="wp-caption-text">SITE123’s live chat support feature</figcaption></figure> I ended up redoing that page as a basic text page, rather than using an About page layout, to remedy the issue. 
<p></p> What SITE123 lacks in design freedom is made up for in a few other significant benefits. <strong>The predetermined layouts ensure that your site is aesthetically pleasing, no matter what</strong> &#8211; you won’t mess up the feel of your whole site because something is misaligned by a fraction of an inch. 
<figure id="attachment_1515864" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1515864"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:54.690491384812% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/site123-page-layouts.png"  width="1567" height="857" alt="SITE123 offers dozens of page layouts to help build your site" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/site123-page-layouts.png"   width="1567" height="857" alt="SITE123 offers dozens of page layouts to help build your site" class="wp-image-1515864 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1515864"class="wp-caption-text">SITE123 offers dozens of page layouts to help build your site</figcaption></figure> In addition, fewer places to change colors and fonts means you spend more time on your site content and less time wondering if this shade or that other one is closer to what you want. This simplicity also leads to faster load speeds on both desktop and mobile, which is critical for a good site experience. 
<h4>Pricing</h4>
<p></p> <strong>SITE123 also has a fairly robust free plan</strong>, and the lowest-tier premium plan adds a lot more storage, a free domain name, and e-commerce capabilities. You’ll also find a lot more customization options if you want more design freedom. <strong>It’s a good value option for a lot of blogs and small businesses</strong>.

<h4>Other Features</h4>
<p></p> SITE123 doesn’t have a ton of extra features, but it does cover the basics that most site builders offer, and in a simpler manner than others. Here are some of those: 
<ul>
<li><strong>SEO</strong>: You can add your title tag, meta description, and image alt text, but that’s about it. There’s also a keyword meta tag field, but that’s pretty obsolete in SEO, so more of an unnecessary inclusion than a real feature.</li>
<li><strong>Online Store</strong>: The online store is pretty thorough in terms of adding product information, and felt very easy to move through as someone who has never set up e-commerce sites before. It comes as a built-in page type on the premium plan or higher, so you don’t have to add anything extra to get started.</li>
<li><strong>Single-page Website</strong>: Although this feature gave me the most trouble at first, SITE123 is certainly the easiest builder for making a single page site with distinct sections and automatic navigation links throughout the page. It’s a great option for portfolios and resumes or event websites that only require a single page.</li>
</ul>

<h3><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=2413&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_2413_top10_145_483189&post_id=145&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="2413" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_2413_top10_145_483189', 'squarespace', this,  true  );">#3 Squarespace &#8211; The Best Website Builder for Design</a></h3>
<figure id="attachment_1520461" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1520461"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:60.549777117385% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-squarespace-2.png"  width="1346" height="815" alt="best-website-builders-squarespace-2" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-squarespace-2.png"   width="1346" height="815" alt="best-website-builders-squarespace-2" class="border wp-image-1520461 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1520461"class="wp-caption-text">My Squarespace test website homepage (Template: Fillmore)</figcaption></figure>

<h4>Ease of Use</h4>
<p></p> Squarespace is one of the easier block editors to use, bringing to mind a hybrid of Wix and WordPress.com. <strong>Moving between the different pieces of the block editor feels smoother and more natural than WordPress.com</strong>, and everything is a bit easier to find. 
<figure id="attachment_1516025" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1516025"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 422px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:126.54028436019% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/squarespace-block-editor.png"  width="422" height="534" alt="The Squarespace block editor has tons of options for your page layout" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/squarespace-block-editor.png"   width="422" height="534" alt="The Squarespace block editor has tons of options for your page layout" class="border wp-image-1516025 size-full ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1516025"class="wp-caption-text">The Squarespace block editor has tons of options for your page layout</figcaption></figure> Upon starting, the Assistant feature gives you a checklist of everything you need to get your site started, and can be called upon or hidden as you need (or don’t need) it. It walks you through basic steps for website setup and links you to the relevant guide for as much information as you need. <strong>Most website builders have some form of tutorial, but Squarespace’s was certainly the most helpful</strong>. 
<p></p> One small but very helpful feature is the ability to bounce back and forth between the live site preview and editor in a single window, unlike SITE123 and other editors that open tab after tab any time you want to preview a change. 
<h4>Design Flexibility</h4>
<p></p> <strong>Squarespace has some of the best templates in the industry</strong>, and they’re on par with the average WordPress.com theme in terms of design flexibility. You can’t change every single color like you can on Wix, and you have some natural limitations by way of the block editor, but overall you can do a ton of customization, and it’s built so that anything you do looks pretty spectacular. 
<p></p> One of my favorite design features is the color palette picker, where you choose three basic colors to match your site, and Squarespace generates broader color themes to be used throughout. Here’s the color palette for my Squarespace test site: 
<figure id="attachment_1516058" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1516058"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 306px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:47.712418300654% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/squarespace-color-palette-designer.png"  width="306" height="146" alt="Choose your base colors with Squarespace’s color palette designer" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/squarespace-color-palette-designer.png"   width="306" height="146" alt="Choose your base colors with Squarespace’s color palette designer" class="wp-image-1516058 size-full ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1516058"class="wp-caption-text">Choose your base colors with Squarespace’s color palette designer</figcaption></figure> And here are the themes it generated: 
<figure id="attachment_1516089" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1516089"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 294px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:192.85714285714% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/squarespace-generates-color-combinations.png"  width="294" height="567" alt="Squarespace generates color combinations for you to use throughout your site" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/squarespace-generates-color-combinations.png"   width="294" height="567" alt="Squarespace generates color combinations for you to use throughout your site" class="wp-image-1516089 size-full ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1516089"class="wp-caption-text">Squarespace generates color combinations for you to use throughout your site</figcaption></figure> You can edit these color themes more heavily, but <strong>sticking to them ensures that you have a designer’s eye on your color palette, even if you’re not a designer yourself</strong>. You don’t have to wonder if that color font looks good on that color background, because Squarespace is telling you: these ones do. 
<h4>Pricing</h4>
<p></p> Squarespace doesn’t have a free plan, but you get a lot of features even on the lower tiers. <strong>You can also test it out with a free 14-day trial</strong> before committing to the paid plan. As you move up in price point, you’ll get more advanced e-commerce features, so smaller blogs and online stores can use Squarespace affordably. The advanced e-commerce plans are generally a bit more affordable than those of e-commerce-specific builders. 
<p></p> Overall, it seems like <strong>Squarespace is committed to ensuring you have the best possible site</strong>, and they know a free plan just won’t cut it to get you the best experience and website there is.

<h4>Other Features</h4>
<p></p> Squarespace’s strongest point is its designs, but there are a few other points worth noting: 
<ul>
<li><strong>Online Store</strong>: Adding products is a bit less intuitive than the store setups on other regular site builders, but it’s on par with the e-commerce-specific builders. After testing all of these builders and learning a lot about online stores, I’ve noticed that the more advanced and capable e-commerce functions come with a steeper learning curve. That’s true of Squarespace as well.</li>
<li><strong>Built-in Email Campaigns</strong>: When you publish a post, you can start building an email campaign with their email feature directly from the post. This is easily the most integrated email capability out of any of the website builders &#8211; you don’t have to add any integrations or extensions to access this.</li>
<li><strong>Other Marketing Features</strong>: The SEO features are pretty standard for a website builder, but there are a few other standout marketing features. There are direct integrations with Instagram, Facebook, and Pinterest, and even a URL builder to help you track paid search campaigns.</li>
</ul>

<h3><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=1685066&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_1685066_top10_145_889880&post_id=145&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="1685066" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_1685066_top10_145_889880', 'webador', this,  true  );">#4 Webador – The Fastest Builder for Beginners</a></h3>
<figure id="attachment_3196541" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196541"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:58.375% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-1.png"  width="1600" height="934" alt="Webador Do Dah Man Homepage." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-1.png"   width="1600" height="934" alt="Webador Do Dah Man Homepage." class="border wp-image-3196541 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196541"class="wp-caption-text">My Webador website homepage.</figcaption></figure>

<h4><strong>Ease of Use</strong></h4>
<p></p> <strong>Setting up a website with Webador is pretty straightforward.</strong> Even if you don’t have any previous experience with website builders, it won’t take you more than 10 minutes to figure out how to create a website in Webador. If you do have previous experience, a brief glance should be enough. 
<p></p> The user interface (UI) is intuitive and clearly labeled to help you edit the different aspects of your site quickly. The <i>S</i><i>ettings</i>, <i>Webshop</i>, <i>Pages</i>, <i>Design</i>, and <i>Editor</i> tabs do exactly what you’d expect them to do. <strong>In particular, t</strong><strong>he design tab is great for making broad changes to the overall mood of your site quickly.</strong> There, you can change the color scheme and fonts of your site to suit your desired tone. 
<figure id="attachment_3196570" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196570"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:49.375% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-2.png"  width="1600" height="790" alt="Webador Design Tab." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-2.png"   width="1600" height="790" alt="Webador Design Tab." class="border wp-image-3196570 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196570"class="wp-caption-text">It only takes a couple of clicks to change your site style completely.</figcaption></figure> Not only that, but Webador’s responsive and back-to-basics editor helps you create a fully-fledged website almost immediately. Overall, Webador is not only easy but <i>blazingly fast</i><i>.</i><i> </i>Thanks to its simple and intuitive tools, this website builder can help anyone (regardless of experience) create a simple website in under 20 minutes. 
<h4><strong>Design Flexibility</strong></h4>
<p></p> Though it can help you create a simple website in minutes, Webador might not be the ideal choice for anything more complex than a few static pages and a blog. That’s because other than a couple of surprising options for media sharing, the editor doesn’t offer that many customization tools. 
<p></p> That’s not to say that it offers nothing of value. <strong>Webador lets you add headings, text, images, buttons, and every other essential element you need to create a working site. </strong>But you won’t find anything remarkable like animation options or layered editing features. If you want to add new elements to a page, Webador will automatically arrange them to a simple grid, which can prevent your site from looking disorganized, but it can also make it look rigid and a little outdated. 
<figure id="attachment_3196599" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196599"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:47% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-3.png"  width="1600" height="752" alt="Webador drag and drop editor." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-3.png"   width="1600" height="752" alt="Webador drag and drop editor." class="border wp-image-3196599 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196599"class="wp-caption-text">Webador offers very basic options for site customization.</figcaption></figure> However, it’s not all bad. Even though it doesn’t include that many flashy add-on features, Webador provides you with all the fundamentals to create a good, simple site. <strong>It also provides a couple of interesting widgets</strong> I didn&#8217;t expect to see, such as file-sharing options and customized visitor forms. 
<h4><strong>E-commerce Features</strong></h4>
<p></p> For a builder with simplicity as its main focus, Webador offers a surprisingly well-rounded set of e-commerce features to help you sell directly from your site. Webador offers options for special tags, discounts, SEO, and more. <strong>It’s also one of the few website builders that don’t charge any transaction fees.</strong> This means you get to keep everything you earn when you set up your online store. 
<p></p> Webador is unlikely to help you build the next multinational e-commerce empire. But if you’re looking to set up a quality store quickly, it’s an excellent choice. 
<h4><strong>Pricing</strong></h4>
<p></p> Webador is one of the cheapest builders on the market. In fact, regardless of which plan you choose, you get the first three months for just $1 per month. Even once the renewal fees start, <strong>Webador remains affordable.</strong>

<p></p> The free plan is great for testing out the editor and deciding if it’s right for you. <strong>However, if you’re ready to make the commitment, </strong>you should opt for Pro, since it allows you to access Webador’s full suite of features and removes advertisements from your site. 
<p></p> You can sell up to 10 products on your site with the Pro plan. If you want more, the Business plan offers everything the Pro plan does, but it allows you to sell an unlimited number of products. 
<h4><strong>Other Features</strong></h4>
<p></p> Webador isn’t the most feature-packed builder out there, but it still manages to fit in a couple of surprises in its relatively limited offering, such as: 
<ul>
<li><strong>Unique file-sharing widgets: </strong>Webador includes options to let you turn your website into a file-sharing hub with a one-button downloader, audio playback, and a document viewer.</li>
<li><strong>Customizable forms: </strong>You can create and modify customized forms to ask visitors for their opinions on various topics. Webador also automatically organizes the results for you.</li>
<li><strong>Drag-and-drop rating system: </strong>If you want an even quicker way to know how your visitors feel about something, you can add responsive, five-star system ratings anywhere on your site.</li>
<li><strong>Easy SEO options: </strong>Webador allows you to customize your site’s SEO easily to help you get more traffic.</li>
</ul>

<figure id="attachment_2513588" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-2513588"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:45.176470588235% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/ionos-featured-image-optimage2.png"  width="850" height="384" alt="ionos-featured-image" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/ionos-featured-image-optimage2.png"   width="850" height="384" alt="ionos-featured-image" class="wp-image-2513588 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-2513588"class="wp-caption-text">My IONOS 1&amp;1 test website homepage (template: business)</figcaption></figure>

<h4>Ease of Use</h4>
<p></p> IONOS has two different site builders: MyWebsite Now and MyWebsite Creator. Since the latter is primarily targeted at experienced developers and designers, I focused on MyWebsite Now as the beginner-friendly option. As it turns out, MyWebsite Now is really, really ease to use. 
<p></p> Set-up is super simple. You just need to select a template and get clicking. <strong>It doesn’t take long to come to grips with MyWebsite Now</strong>, especially if you’ve used a site builder before. 
<p></p> I did, however, occasionally find myself a bit confused with the way IONOS works. For instance, <strong>there’s a separation between adding things and editing them</strong>. You have to enter the <em>Section editor</em> to add something to your section (say, a button), then go back a step to customize it. It&#8217;s fine once you figure it out, albeit a bit counter-intuitive. 
<figure id="attachment_2487902" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-2487902"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:45.294117647059% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/ionos-section-options-optimage2.png"  width="850" height="385" alt="ionos-section-options" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/ionos-section-options-optimage2.png"   width="850" height="385" alt="ionos-section-options" class="border wp-image-2487902 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-2487902"class="wp-caption-text">The idea of section options threw me for a while, but it’s simple enough once you get used to it.</figcaption></figure> Overall, though, this was barely a learning curve; more of a learning blip. MyWebsite Now lets you assemble your site using pre-made content blocks. You add a section like a gallery, a grid, or a contact form, choose the layout you prefer, and then edit the text and images. 
<p></p> There is no endless tweaking to make things look right. I was happy at how quickly I could put my site together in this way. It was fast and simple. 
<p></p> If you ever run into issues, there’s a big knowledgebase with lots of tutorials, tips, and tricks. There’s also customer support on the phone. 
<h4>Design Flexibility</h4>
<p></p> The MyWebsite Now builder has a selection of well-designed templates that are clean, modern, and mobile-friendly &#8211; there just aren&#8217;t many of them. Only 18 designs are available, basically one per industry. It&#8217;s not a lot of options, but it&#8217;s possible to make each your own. 
<p></p> <strong>For a simple website builder, IONOS gives you a pretty good range of personalization options</strong>. You can set colors and fonts to apply across your entire website &#8211; there’s also an option to create your own custom color palette &#8211; as well as customize each element individually in terms of colors, fonts, and spacing. 
<figure id="attachment_2487939" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-2487939"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:45.529411764706% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/ionos-customization-options-optimage2.png"  width="850" height="387" alt="ionos-customization-options" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/ionos-customization-options-optimage2.png"   width="850" height="387" alt="ionos-customization-options" class="border wp-image-2487939 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-2487939"class="wp-caption-text">The ability to set custom palettes felt like a bonus to me for a simple site builder.</figcaption></figure> <strong>The only thing I really missed was the option to drag and drop elements wherever I wanted</strong>. You can&#8217;t, for instance, drag a button into the middle of a pre-designed block of content. You can insert one &#8211; sometimes(!) &#8211; and only where IONOS thinks it’s okay to do so. It’s not a deal-breaker, but it meant I couldn’t quite get my site looking <em>exactly</em> the way I wanted. 
<p></p> There are more customization options on the MyWebsite Creator builder, but the latter is less suitable for beginners. 
<h3>E-commerce Features</h3>
<p></p> IONOS gives you the option to upgrade for e-commerce features &#8211; and it is one of the cheapest e-commerce plans out there. If you want a simple online store, this is good value for money. 
<p></p> As you’d expect from the price, the e-commerce tools aren’t as robust as what you’d get with a dedicated e-commerce builder like Shopify or BigCommerce. But you do get light inventory management, product options, tax and shipping settings, and a content block for adding related products to your product pages. You can also sell both digital and physical goods. 
<p></p> IONOS also lets you create discounts and coupons, set up abandoned cart emails, and use integrations to sell directly from your site via Facebook, Instagram, Google Shopping, eBay, and Amazon. Some builders on this list reserve these features for premium e-commerce plans, but IONOS includes them as standard. 
<h3>Pricing</h3>
<p></p> If you’re opting for MyWebsite Now (which is my recommendation for a beginner), there are two plans: Starter and Online Store Starter. The right one for you simply depends on whether you want to sell online. 
<p></p> <strong>Starter comes with all the templates, design options, color schemes, a free domain for one year, and a professional email.</strong> The Online Store Starter plan throws in online store tools like product listings, payment options, shipping and collection options, marketing tools, and integrations for selling your products via social media. 
<p></p> You can try the builder at no cost &#8211; kind of. It&#8217;s a bit frustrating, but IONOS only offers no-cost plans to those who choose monthly subscriptions. If you opt for a yearly plan (which ends up being much less expensive), you don&#8217;t receive the free month but rather a reduced price for your initial 12 months. 
<p></p> You do, however, get a 30-day money-back guarantee, so either way, you can cancel within 30 days for a full refund. But it would be nice not to have to get out your credit card to sign up. Just saying. 
<h3>Other features</h3>
<p></p> IONOS isn’t exactly flush with extra features. There’s no app market for adding functionality, for example &#8211; but it does have most of the basics, including: 
<ul>
<li><strong>SEO tools</strong>: MyWebsite Now comes with some basic SEO tools, including setting page names, descriptions, and images for social media sharing.</li>
<li><strong>Analytics</strong>: You can keep track of visitors to your site with IONOS’ simple inbuilt analytics tool.</li>
<li><strong>GDPR</strong>: The pre-built cookie banner is a super simple way to make sure your website is GDPR-compliant.</li>
<li><strong>Image library</strong>: You can access a library of more than 17,000 royalty-free images, to help make your site visual even if you don’t have top photography skills.</li>
</ul>

<figure id="attachment_1516759" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1516759"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:60.598345003183% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-shopify.png"  width="1571" height="952" alt="My Shopify website homepage" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/best-website-builders-shopify.png"   width="1571" height="952" alt="My Shopify website homepage" class="border wp-image-1516759 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1516759"class="wp-caption-text">My Shopify website homepage</figcaption></figure>

<h4>Ease of Use</h4>
<p></p> <strong>Shopify has many features that are easy to use, but the style of the editor changes depending on what you’re working on, which isn’t an ideal experience</strong>. The homepage editor is a block-type editor like SITE123 or Jimdo, but every other page is edited in a text-based format that’s reminiscent of the pre-Gutenberg WordPress editor. 
<figure id="attachment_1516789" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1516789"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:61.228813559322% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/shopify-page-editor.png"  width="944" height="578" alt="Shopify page editor" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/shopify-page-editor.png"   width="944" height="578" alt="Shopify page editor" class="border wp-image-1516789 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1516789"class="wp-caption-text">Shopify page editor</figcaption></figure> The product manager and editor has a similar feel, so it doesn’t come across quite as modern as the e-commerce options on other builders. The app I used for the photo gallery on <strong>my Shopify test site</strong> had an even more outdated feel, but as with most external apps, that could have just been chance. 
<p></p> <strong>Despite the older feel of some of the editing options, it’s still fairly simple to navigate and find what you need</strong>. Blocks and apps are well-categorized and clearly labeled, and you can sort and filter your products by a lot of different criteria. 
<p></p> <strong>Shopify also has a robust support section, so anything that is more difficult to accomplish</strong> can be easily found in the help center. 
<h4>Design Flexibility</h4>
<p></p> <strong>Shopify has a lot of color and font options to customize your theme, as well as a strong selection of blocks</strong><strong> from which you can build your homepage</strong>. The layout flexibility doesn’t extend to other pages, but a handful of the thousands of available apps are page builders which may provide additional design flexibility to some store pages. (However, if you need a lot of site content and a lot of online store capability, you likely need a different website builder anyway.) 
<h4>E-Commerce Features</h4>
<p></p> Shopify’s e-commerce features are intended to benefit brick-and-mortar retailers as well, so they have some cool features for adding locations and tracking inventory at each store, as well as transfers to and from locations. 
<figure id="attachment_1516818" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1516818"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:59.642591213701% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/shopify-inventory-tracking-layout.png"  width="1343" height="801" alt="Shopify’s inventory tracking layout" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/shopify-inventory-tracking-layout.png"   width="1343" height="801" alt="Shopify’s inventory tracking layout" class="border wp-image-1516818 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1516818"class="wp-caption-text">Shopify’s inventory tracking layout</figcaption></figure> Beyond that, they offer ways of tracking products, inventory, and variants that are similar to Square Online and BigCommerce. Overall, Shopify offers a robust e-commerce building experience. 
<h4>Pricing</h4>
<p></p> All of the e-commerce builders have similar pricing structures, but Shopify gives you a bit more bang for your buck (<strong>there’s also a free trial</strong>). You can get massive shipping discounts, the ability to add store locations, and a few other goodies for essentially the same price as BigCommerce. 
<div class="pricing-vendor" ><div class="pricing-vendor-item"><a class="clickoutLink" rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" <h3><a href="https://www.websiteplanet.com/goto.php?id=1909&lang=en&deep_id=0&deep_name=&btn_name=VendorExternalUrl_1909_top10_145_889891&post_id=145&pageview_id=0&direct_link=&type=top10&amp=0"  rel="sponsored noopener norefferer" data-id="1909" class="clickoutLink boldLink shortC" target="_blank" onclick="trackClickout('event', 'clickout', 'VendorExternalUrl_1909_top10_145_889891', 'web-com', this,  true  );">#7 Web.com – A Well-Rounded Option for Intermediate Users</a></h3>
<figure id="attachment_3196628" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196628"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:63.1875% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-4.png"  width="1600" height="1011" alt="Web.com Do Dah Man." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-4.png"   width="1600" height="1011" alt="Web.com Do Dah Man." class="border wp-image-3196628 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196628"class="wp-caption-text">My Web.com website homepage.</figcaption></figure>

<h4><strong>Ease of Use</strong></h4>
<p></p> You don’t have to be a professional website designer to get the hang of Web.com. However, I wouldn’t recommend it as the most beginner-friendly option nor as a quick and easy tool for building a website in a couple of minutes. That’s not even due to a particularly steep learning curve. Theoretically, you <i>could </i>create a very simple site in a few steps, but <strong>the features that really make Web.com worth it require a little more technical expertise.</strong> 
<p></p> <strong>Web.com places a lot of emphasis on tools for things like spacing, nested design, and responsiveness.</strong> All of these can make a big difference in creating the right design for your site but might seem unnecessary and overly technical if you’re not interested in the design details. 
<p></p> This puts Web.com in a bit of an awkward position, as it’s a little too complex for complete beginners but lacks advanced features that professional designers and agencies would want. However, <strong>it implements its tools in an accessible and intuitive way, making it a great builder for getting started with design concepts</strong>. 
<figure id="attachment_3196657" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196657"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:55.1875% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-5.png"  width="1600" height="883" alt="Web.com spacing tools." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-5.png"   width="1600" height="883" alt="Web.com spacing tools." class="border wp-image-3196657 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196657"class="wp-caption-text">Web.com makes it easy to fine-tune spacing and layout details.</figcaption></figure> The editor can get glitchy, and its user interface isn’t quite as intuitive as Wix’s or Squarespace’s, but<strong> Web.com offers an advanced, accessible editor for web design intermediates.</strong> 
<h4><strong>Design Flexibility</strong></h4>
<p></p> If you’re willing to invest the proper amount of time into your site, <strong>Web.com can help you create any design you imagine</strong>. Thanks to its well-structured editor, you can start with the big picture and then focus on the details of each element. 
<p></p> For starters, Web.com has a wide selection of over 200 professionally designed templates to fit a wide variety of needs. 
<p></p> Once you’ve selected your ideal starting point, you can modify all the general aspects of your site’s look from the <i>Theme</i> tab. Its design options go beyond the usual color and font choices. <strong>Web.com allows you to fine-tune the style of your site’s buttons, headings, dividers, and even timelines and countdowns.</strong> 
<p></p> If you want to make sure that your style is particularly <i>on-brand</i>, Web.com offers a color wizard tool. All you have to do is upload your logo to the color wizard, and it will automatically update all site colors to match your logo’s palette. 
<p></p> But Web.com really shines when it comes to individual widgets or blocks. Not only is its widget selection considerably more diverse than the competition (with widgets for things like custom countdowns, progress bars, and interactive maps), but <strong>it also gives you an incredible amount of control over each element’s design.</strong> 
<figure id="attachment_3196686" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196686"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:48.625% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-6.png"  width="1600" height="778" alt="Web.com customization features." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-6.png"   width="1600" height="778" alt="Web.com customization features." class="border wp-image-3196686 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196686"class="wp-caption-text">Web.com helps you ensure that every part of your website looks “just right”.</figcaption></figure> Its lack of integration with any sort of app market is a bit disappointing, and while having access to so many design features is mostly a good thing, it can also get overwhelming. Still, <strong>I’d choose a builder that gives me too much control over one that gives me too little any day of the week.</strong> 
<h4><strong>E-commerce Features</strong></h4>
<p></p> While sales aren’t its main focus, Web.com still offers a fairly complete set of e-commerce capabilities. Its e-commerce dashboard is user-friendly and fairly robust, and <strong>since it’s separate from the design dashboard, it helps you focus on running a functional online store.</strong> 
<p></p> For each new product, you can add as many details and specifications as you want, both for your customers’ convenience and to help keep track of item performance. You can also input information about orders, shipments, and even tax rules to your dashboard. <strong>With all this data, you can use</strong><strong> Web.com’s pre-made business reports</strong><strong> to track your business’s health and pain spots.</strong> 
<p></p> The payment method selection is still somewhat limited, and there are no customized reports. Even then, Web.com’s offering for online businesses is impressive. 
<h4><strong>Pricing</strong></h4>
<p></p> If all you want is to create a website tailor-made to your vision, Web.com’s Website Essentials offers a lot more in terms of features and customization than many other starting plans on the market. <strong>In fact, if you’re not interested in e-commerce capabilities, Website Essentials offers all you need</strong><strong> – at an affordable rate</strong><strong>.</strong> 
<p></p> <strong>Beyond that, it’s all about e-commerce and growth.</strong> The Business Essentials plan adds powerful marketing and SEO features to help you get found online. The eCommerce Essentials and eCommerce Premium plans allow you to sell products online through multiple sales channels and give you access to branding features.

<p></p> Though it’s a fairly impressive offering overall, <strong>keep in mind that there are steep renewal costs for each plan.</strong> Especially considering Web.com’s plans include a free domain name and an SSL certificate only for the first year. When you renew, you’ll have to pay three separate upcharges. The end price isn’t terrible, but the extra costs <i>are</i> worth thinking about before you make a long-term commitment to Web.com. 
<h4><strong>Other Features</strong></h4>
<p></p> Web.com offers a pleasantly-surprising toolbox filled with web-building goodies. All the extra features available outside of its website building plan only add to its value. Here are my favorites: 
<ul>
<li><strong>Quickstart: </strong>If you’d rather leave the heavy lifting to the professionals, you can. With Web.com’s Quickstart service, professional designers create your website for you based on your needs and vision. Once they’re done, you can use the classic editor to make changes.</li>
<li><strong>Template generation wizard: </strong>If you don’t feel like spending hours looking for the perfect template, you can instead answer a few questions about your website and let the template generation wizard create a customized starting point for you.</li>
<li><strong>Pre-made blocks: </strong>As you edit your site, you don’t have to add each element individually to get the ideal result. Web.com offers a wide selection of pre-generated widget blocks for things like contact forms, testimonials, and image galleries.</li>
<li><strong>Logo builder:</strong> As a side service, Web.com offers an easy-to-use logo builder which you can use to build a unique identity for your brand.</li>
</ul>

<h4>Ease of Use</h4>
<p></p> WordPress.com’s Gutenberg block editor is somewhat easy to use if you understand the concept of using blocks to create layouts. <strong>You can start building a page from an existing template</strong><strong> to streamline your design experience</strong>, and there are dozens of block types to choose from. These are helpfully categorized by their purpose, so you don’t have to spend a lot of time hunting for what you need. 
<figure id="attachment_1515924" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1515924"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 329px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:139.81762917933% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/wordpress-com-blocks.png"  width="329" height="460" alt="WordPress.com has dozens of blocks to choose from" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/wordpress-com-blocks.png"   width="329" height="460" alt="WordPress.com has dozens of blocks to choose from" class="border wp-image-1515924 size-full ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1515924"class="wp-caption-text">WordPress.com has dozens of blocks to choose from</figcaption></figure> More so than the other block editors on this list, I found this one to be a bit annoying. It sometimes placed blocks slightly off alignment for no reason that I could determine, meaning <strong>I had to rework parts of the page or copy existing blocks to get it to work correctly</strong>. This isn’t insurmountable, but happens just often enough to be annoying. 
<p></p> On the Business plan or higher, you do have the option to install Elementor, a plugin that creates a drag-and-drop editor experience. 
<p></p> <strong>While everything within the editor is clearly labeled, it often feels like you have to jump around a bit to get everything for a single page done</strong>. For example, to edit the background color, you have to leave the block editor and go to the customizer and then back, which feels a bit disjointed, especially compared to other website builders where every customization and change can be done in the same interface. 
<h4>Design Flexibility</h4>
<p></p> Customization options vary widely and are entirely dependent on the theme you choose. My first theme wouldn’t even let me change colors or fonts, but the second one I chose allowed far more options. In general, the more recent themes by WordPress<strong> allow greater flexibility</strong> &#8211; I used one called Twenty Twenty for my WordPress test site &#8211; while third-party themes are hit-or-miss in those capabilities. 
<figure id="attachment_1515958" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-1515958"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-smallimg-wrapper " style="max-width: 309px"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:136.56957928803% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/wordpress-com-customizer.png"  width="309" height="422" alt="WordPress.com’s customizer varies based on your template" /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/wordpress-com-customizer.png"   width="309" height="422" alt="WordPress.com’s customizer varies based on your template" class="border wp-image-1515958 size-full ll-img"/></span></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-1515958"class="wp-caption-text">WordPress.com’s customizer varies based on your template</figcaption></figure> There are page templates available to jumpstart your design, but you can also start with a completely blank page and add blocks in whatever arrangement you like. There’s a good balance of freedom and guidance when it comes to design flexibility: <strong>if you’re building your first website, you won’t feel like you have to suddenly master web design</strong>, and if you’re an experienced designer, you won’t feel limited by existing templates. 
<p></p> WordPress.com’s flexibility extends to functionality as well, with <strong>thousands of plugins available to add analytics, contact forms, SEO, and almost anything you can think of</strong>. The plugins are largely compatible with the block editor, although as with the themes, those by third-party creators may have some limitations on what they can do. (Keep in mind that you do need a Business plan or higher to install plugins.) 
<h4>Pricing</h4>
<p></p> WordPress.com has one of the widest ranges of prices <strong>(there’s also a free plan available)</strong>, and there are significant distinctions between each plan. <strong>The lowest tiers are very affordable, and are sufficient for bloggers or freelancers</strong> who need a highly functional but low cost website. The Business plan is needed to access plugins, custom themes, and other advanced features, but with everything it offers, it is well worth the cost.

<h4>Other Features</h4>
<p></p> Plugins make up a lot of WordPress.com’s best features, but there were a few small built-in things that were convenient and I didn’t see in other site builders: 
<ul>
<li>Image attribution from Pexels and other stock sites are automatically added</li>
<li>Videos can be directly uploaded</li>
<li>Most import/export options between platforms</li>
<li>Fastest load speeds on desktop and mobile</li>
</ul>

<figure id="attachment_3196715" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-3196715"class="wp-caption aligncenter"><span class="ll-img-wrapper "  style="padding:53.5625% 0 0; max-width: 850px;"><noscript><img src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-7.png"  width="1600" height="857" alt="Duda Do Dah Mann." /></noscript><img data-src="https://dt2sdf0db8zob.cloudfront.net/wp-content/uploads/2023/11/image-issue-7.png"   width="1600" height="857" alt="Duda Do Dah Mann." class="border wp-image-3196715 size-full ll-img"/></span><figcaption id="caption-attachment-3196715"class="wp-caption-text">My Duda website homepage.</figcaption></figure>
